return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref18" aria-label="reference 18">18</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped carbon nanoribbons</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">poly pyrrole</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">2230</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">711</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">20</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">6</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">hierarchical porous carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">tea waste</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">337</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.372</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">244</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref33" aria-label="reference 33">33</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">7</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-carbon/rGO nanosheets</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">pyrrole coated GO</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">327</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">554</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref37'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref37" aria-label="reference 37">37</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">8</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped Carbon nanospheres</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">lignin</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">419.2</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.06</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">225</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39" aria-label="reference 39">39</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">9</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped porous carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">shrimp shells</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">1271</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">1.0</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">480</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref40" aria-label="reference 40">40</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">10</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped porous carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">porous polymer</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">1845</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.550</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">408</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42" aria-label="reference 42">42</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="left">11</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped porous carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">TPPA based COFs</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">482</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">506</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">43</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" scope="row" align="left">12</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">N-rich spherical carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">PD-triazine based COF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="char" char=".">390</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">785</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">present work</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">0.5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">623</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></div><div id="sec3_3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i10" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i10"> Electrochemical Performance As an Anode in SIBs</h3><div class="NLM_p">The N-rich SC particle can also be a promising anode for SIBs, where the large interlayer distance can accommodate sodium ions. Na-ion insertion and extraction behavior of N-rich spherical carbon were investigated by both cyclic voltammetry and galvanostatic charge/discharge cycling studies. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>a depicts the ten consecutive CV curves cycled between 2.5 and 0.01 V at a scan rate of 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. In the first cathodic scan, three irreversible broad cathodic peaks can be observed at approximately ∼1.4, 0.98, and 0.54 V. The peak at 1.4 V reflects the interaction between sodium ions and the oxygen containing functional groups. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27 ref34'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27 ref34" aria-label="reference 27 and 34">(27, 34)</a> The peak at 0.98 and 0.54 V are ascribed to the electrolyte decomposition on different active sites and subsequent SEI formation. In the subsequent cycles (up to 10 cycles), the CV curves almost overlapped suggesting the stable and excellent reversibility of the present system. A pair of sharp redox peak observed at 0.01 and 0.11 V indicates minimum hysteresis of sodium insertion and extraction at the interlayer of the nongraphitic moiety. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref27" aria-label="reference 27">(27)</a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>b and c represent the galvanostatic charge/discharge cycling profile and steady state cycling studies of N-doped SC particle at a current density of 0.1 Ag<sup>–1</sup> up to 100 cycles. The material initially delivered a steady state discharge capacity of about 291 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> up to 51 cycles and steadily increased to 307 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> which could be ascribed to partial activation of N-doped porous carbon particle. The steady state cycling performance at a high current density (0.5 Ag<sup>–1</sup>) is shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>d, which exhibits an average discharge capacity of about 238 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> for the studied 500 cycles. Selected charge/discharge cycling profiles at a current density of 0.1 and 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">SI Figure S8a and b</a>. The charge/discharge cycling profiles for formation cycle and at different current densities are shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">SI Figure S9a and b</a>. In the formation cycle (0.025 A g<sup>–1</sup>), the discharge and charge capacities are 689 and 387 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> respectively with 56% Coulombic efficiency. The irreversible capacity loss arising from both the electrolyte decomposition as well as sodium ion insertion at the irreversible sites correlates with the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> into parallelly aligned carbon nanosheets and nanopore filling. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53 ref54'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref53 ref54" aria-label="reference 53 and 54">(53, 54)</a> As shown in <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">SI Figure S9c</a>, the derivative of discharge curve clearly exhibiting two distinct slopes, plateau at the high potential range can be endorsed to insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> ions between the graphene like carbon nanosheets where the narrow low voltage (close to sodium plating) ascribed to Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption at sp<sup>2</sup> configured meso-micropores. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref3 ref53'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref3 ref53" aria-label="reference 3 and 53">(3, 53)</a> The plateau observed at 0.1 V in charging curve corresponds to sodium extraction and the result is consistent with the anodic peak observed in the CV curve (0.11 V). Further, no considerable decrease in peak intensity occurs after 50 cycles demonstrating the stability and good reversibility of the present material. To examine the rate capability of the present material in SIBs, the material was cycled at different current densities, and the corresponding Coulombic efficiencies are displayed in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>e. The electrode delivered perceptible average discharge capacities of 340, 306, 260, 230, 192 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a current rates of 0.05, 0.1, 0.25, 0.5, and 1.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> respectively. When the current density was switched back again to 0.05, 0.1 0.5, 2.0, 4.0, and 8.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> the reversible capacity could be recovered to 332, 292, 206, 149, 111, and 46 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> receptively. The rate performance is more impressive, considering after cycling in each current densities. Furthermore, the same cell was tested for steady state cycling study at a current density of 0.75 A g<sup>–1</sup>, which delivered a reversible capacity of 205 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at the initial cycle and attained 233 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> after 200 cycles. The capacity increment after few cycles may be attributed to the activation of electrode material and are common for porous carbon in extended cycling studies. It is noteworthy that the excellent rate performance and cycling stability of the present material deserve for practical application toward proto-type SIB.</div><figure id="fig6" data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/medium/am-2017-10882k_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/large/am-2017-10882k_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Electrochemical performance of N-rich SC in SIBs, (a) Cyclic Voltammetry curves (ten consecutive cycles) at 0.1 mV s<sup>–1</sup> scan rate, (b) Galvanostatic charge/discharge cycling profile obtained at a current density of 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, (c) capacity retention as a function of cycle number, (d) steady state cycling performance at a current density of 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> (e) Rate performance at different current densities from 0.1 to 8.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/large/am-2017-10882k_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b10882&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">High rate charge/discharge cycling studies are important for battery in the practical utilization. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">SI Figure S10</a> depicts the charge/discharge cycling studies at high current densities for N-doped spherical carbon particle. The appreciable average discharge capacities of about 159, 121, and 46 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> have been derived for the studied 250 cycles at current densities of 2.0, 4.0, and 8.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> respectively. It is also noted that the nitrogen rich spherical carbon particle exhibits excellent electrochemical performance as SIBs anode when compared with other nitrogen doped carbon material and are tabulated in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl2" aria-label="Table 2">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl2" href="#tbl2">2</a>. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>a and b explain the rate capability behavior of N-doped SC with other reported materials for LIBs and SIBs, respectively. As compared with other N-doped materials, the synthesized material exhibits excellent rate performance even at high current densities. To compare the rate performance, all the capacities were normalized with the obtained reversible capacity at a low rate and plotted against corresponding current densities. The material shows the reversible capacity of 55% at 4.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> and 44% at 2.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> in rate study for Li/Na ion batteries.</div><figure id="fig7" data-index="7" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 7</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/medium/am-2017-10882k_0007.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/large/am-2017-10882k_0007.jpeg" id="gr7" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 7. (a) and (b) Comparison of rate capability behavior of N-rich SC particles with other reported materials, (c) and (d) EIS spectra of before and after cycling along with fitting for LIBs and SIBs, respectively.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/asset/images/large/am-2017-10882k_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b10882&amp;id=fig7"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl2"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 2. return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36" aria-label="reference 36">36</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="char" char=".">14</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">porous N-doped carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">horn comb</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">1883</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">100</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">241</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref41" aria-label="reference 41">41</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="char" char=".">15</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped porous carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">TPPA based COFs</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">482</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">100</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">228.5</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref43" aria-label="reference 43">43</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" scope="row" align="char" char=".">16</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">N-doped carbon sphere</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left">polypyrrole</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">95.1</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">200</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">215</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="left"> <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref44" aria-label="reference 44">44</a></td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" scope="row" align="char" char=".">17</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">N-rich spherical carbon</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">PD-triazine based COF</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="char" char=".">390</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">100</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">292</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" rowspan="2" align="left">present work</td></tr><tr valign="top" class="colsep0"><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">500</td><td class="colsep0 rowsep0" align="char" char=".">238</td></tr></tbody></table></div></div><div class="NLM_p">To understand the excellent rate performance of the synthesized N-rich spherical particle, the electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were carried out before and after cycling and fitted with ZMAN 2.2 fitting software, which is shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>c and d. The Nyquist plots obtained from LIBs and SIBs consist of two partially overlapped depressed semicircle at high-middle and an inclined line at low frequency. The semicircle observed at high frequency region can be attributed to SEI formation (<i>R</i><sub>f</sub>), and the intercept with Z′ axis corresponds to contact/Ohmic resistance (R<sub>s</sub>), while at middle frequency region endorses to charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and constant phase element (CPE). Further, the inclined line refers Warburg resistance (W) and is related to Li<sup>+</sup>/Na<sup>+</sup> ion diffusion, where this low frequency intercept explains the activation kinetics at the interface. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig7" aria-label="Figure 7">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig7" id="" class=" internalNav">7</a>c and d depict the typical Nyquist plots before and after cycling along with fitting for LIBs and SIBs respectively, which infers that some obvious difference in (<i>R</i><sub>s</sub>) and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>. In LIBs, the <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> value increased to 5.3 from 4.3 Ω after cycling and the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> changed to 34.2 from 186.3 Ω. Similarly in SIBs, after cycling the <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value changed to 10.4 and 212.8 Ω form 8.9 and 757.3 Ω respectively. The decreased <i>R</i><sub>f</sub> and R<sub>ct</sub> value after cycling could be endorsed to stable SEI, good contact as well as large interface formation due to effective wetting between the electrode and electrolyte leads to enhanced electronic/ionic conductivity. <a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">SI Figure S11</a> explains the Randles equivalent circuit obtained from fitting software. The decrease in discharge capacity at high rates might be attributed to the reduction of cyclable lithium between the electrodes and promotion of SEI growth. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55" aria-label="reference 55">(55)</a></div><div class="NLM_p last">Apparently, the superior electrochemical performance for both LIBs and SIBs, including excellent reversible capacity even at high current densities, good cycling stability and rate capability of the present material could be attributed to large interlayer distance, high level nitrogen doping as well as the existence of a large number of pores and voids.</div></div></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i12">4.0 Conclusions</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, a high level N-doped spherical carbon particles were successfully prepared by facile and scalable synthesis method via. direct carbonization of the N-rich covalent organic molecule. The resultant product contains 10.9 wt % of nitrogen as confirmed by elemental analysis, EDAX and XPS analysis. Furthermore, the uniform grafting of nitrogen in the spherical carbon skeleton was confirmed with elemental mapping, which provides abundant active sites (pyridinic-N or pyrrolic-N) for ion accommodation. The dilated interlayer distance with the high specific surface area and narrow pore size distribution with heteroatom doping exhibits excellent electrochemical performance as an anode in lithium/sodium ion batteries. In LIBs, the N-doped SC particles exhibited a high reversible capacity of about ∼623 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a current density of 0.5 A g<sup>–1</sup> for the studied 500 cycles and 303 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 8.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 250 cycles. Similarly, in SIBs, the same material delivered an average discharge capacity of about 307 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup> after 100 cycles, 128 and 53 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at a high current density of 4.0 and 8.0 A g<sup>–1</sup> respectively after 250 cycles. When compared with existing N-doped nongraphitic materials the CTF derived material shows good electrochemical performance in both LIBs and SIBs, which demonstrates the possibility of an alternative anode for high-rate performance batteries.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="notes-1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i13">Supporting Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><p class="last">The Supporting Information is available free of charge on the <a href="/" class="ext-link">ACS Publications website</a> at DOI: <a href="/doi/abs/10.1021/acsami.7b10882" class="ext-link">10.1021/acsami.7b10882</a>.</p><ul class="NLM_list-list_type-label" id="silist"><li><p class="inline">HR-TEM EDAX mapping, FT-IR, cycling profiles at different current densities and steady state cycling performance at high current densities for both LIBs and SIBs (<a href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf" class="ext-link">PDF</a>)</p></li></ul><p></p><div class="supInfoBoxOnFTP "><div class="sup-info-attachments"><ul><li><a class="suppl-anchor" href="/doi/suppl/10.1021/acsami.7b10882/suppl_file/am7b10882_si_001.pdf">am7b10882_si_001.pdf (1.76 MB)</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b10882" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3" data-pb-dropzone="TermsAndConditionsDropzone3"><div data-widget-def="UX3HTMLWidget" data-widget-id="85b54935-30e9-4058-a6d2-0b40fb754a85" class="mb-4">

        </div><div class="casAbstract">First-principles calcns. were done to examine the energetics of alkali metal intercalation into graphite.  Calcns. based on the exchange-correlation functionals that include a nonlocal correlation were found to give reasonable agreement with expts. concerning the crystal structure of graphite and LiC6, binding energy of graphene sheets, and Li intercalation potential.  We found that K intercalation from KC8 to KC6 cannot be achieved through electrochem. reactions.  We also found that the absence of the stage-I structures for Na graphite intercalation compds. such as NaC6 or NaC8 is linked to a relatively high redox potential of Na/Na+ compared to that of Li/Li+.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrkrh00uHZZmrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhOklERg2S0xQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFOnsbjE&amp;md5=7dd2008870838ff0cd26d7a2c6f782cb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref7"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref7'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">7</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit7" data-doi="10.1021/jp901968v"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yin, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Q.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, T.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Porous Carbon Nanofibers Derived from Conducting Polymer: Synthesis and Application in Lithium-Ion Batteries with High-Rate Capability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.                         cas_cit7R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">7</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous Carbon Nanofibers Derived from Conducting Polymer: Synthesis and Application in Lithium-Ion Batteries with High-Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Chengchao; Yin, Xiaoming; Chen, Libao; Li, Qiuhong; Wang, Taihong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Physical Chemistry C</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoscale porous C fibers (CNFs) were obtained by pyrolysis in an Ar atm. of a conducting polymer synthesized by a self-degrdn. template method.  The diam. and length of the fibers are 100 nm and 2-3 μm, resp.  Owing to the high porosity and conducting 1-dimensional network, these porous C nanofibers show enhanced Li-ion storage properties when used as anode material in Li-ion battery.  The reversible specific capacity of the CNFs at a 0.5 C rate is ∼400 mA-h/g.                         cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Sodium Ion Insertion in Hollow Carbon Nanowires for Battery Applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Cao, Yuliang; Xiao, Lifen; Sushko, Maria L.; Wang, Wei; Schwenzer, Birgit; Xiao, Jie; Nie, Zimin; Saraf, Laxmikant V.; Yang, Zhengguo; Liu, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hollow carbon nanowires were prepd. by pyrolysis of a hollow polyaniline nanowire precursor.  The hollow carbon nanowires used as anode material for Na-ion batteries deliver a high reversible capacity of 251 mA-h/g and 82.2% capacity retention over 400 charge-discharge cycles between 1.2 and 0.01 V (vs. Na+/Na) at a const. current of 50 mA/g (0.2C).                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass derived hard carbon used as a high performance anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Kun-lei; Long, Qie; Zeng, Rui; Yi, Zi-qi; Zhang, Wei; Wang, Duo; Yin, Wei; Wu, Chao; Fan, Qing-jie; Zhang, Wu-xing; Huang, Yun-hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The sodium storage mechanisms of the porous hard carbon can be explained by Na+ intercalation into the disordered graphene layers, redox reaction of the surface O-contg. functional groups and Na+ storage in the nanoscale pores.  However, the porous hard carbon demonstrated a low coulombic efficiency of 27%, resulting from the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase film and the side reactions of surface phosphorus groups.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoldD5kAMcszLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXQLS_klgWLg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVKmtbrO&amp;md5=9b28ca12b1ea3a55e7e2ada7ae1e05f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.09.052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Suryawanshi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mhamane, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nagane, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Patil, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aravindan, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ogale, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Srinivasan, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Indanthrone Derived Disordered Graphitic Carbon as Promising Insertion Anode for Sodium Ion Battery with Long Cycle life</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning with partially carbonization in air: Highly porous carbon nanofibers optimized for high-performance flexible lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weihan; Li, Minsi; Wang, Min; Zeng, Linchao; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-supported and flexible highly porous carbon nanofibers (HPCNFs) were prepd. by electrospinning method combined with a post-two-step carbonization process.  By introduction of air into the Ar flow during carbonization, carbon nanofibers were partially burnt off and a large no. of micro/mesopores were created.  As effective lithium storage units, the porous structure plays an important role in enhancing the electrochem. performances.  The HPCNFs delivers a reversible capacity as high as 1780 mAh g-1 after 40 cycles at 50 mA g-1 and ultralong cycle life (1550 mAh g-1 after 600 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  Even cycled at 25 A g-1, it still displays a very high capacity of 200 mAh g-1.  The outstanding electrochem. and mech. properties of HPCNFs are attributed to the novel structure: pores provide good access of the electrolyte to the electrode surface and facilitate fast charge transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface. 3D interconnected networks decrease the contact resistance and improve elec. cond. of the overall electrode, which enhance electron transport rate.  Therefore, this novel carbon material holds great promise for potential applications in energy-related technol. and flexible electrodes for next generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNd91PVUFXXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXQLS_klgWLg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlslyrs74%253D&amp;md5=0d28e55b2245e971c28e1a64eaf647e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA05451B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Amorphous monodispersed hard carbon micro-spherules derived from biomass as a high performance negative electrode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yunming; Xu, Shuyin; Wu, Xiaoyan; Yu, Juezhi; Wang, Yuesheng; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Li, Hong; Chen, Liquan; Huang, Xuejie</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.  The theor. energy d. of this system is 200 W-h/kg.  These promising properties are believed to be close to the level required for practical applications.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGo1jsHJQCoWPrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXQLS_klgWLg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvVSqs7bK&amp;md5=1d0ab49c7539719d3b644ebc28a2d568</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1039/C5RA01569C"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhao, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, R.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Performance N-doped Porous Activated Carbon based on Chicken Feather for Supercapacitors and CO<sub>2</sub> Capture</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">RSC Adv.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">5</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">34803</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">34811</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A low cost carbon precursor to produce carbon with large sp. surface area and abundant heteroatoms is essential for CO2 uptake and supercapacitors to realize economic viability.  We report a facile synthesis method and superior performance of a kind of porous activated carbon based on chicken feather.  Herein, different activated temps. and alkali/carbon ratios (KOH vs. carbon in g/g) are used to tailor the pore structure and the surface chem., so the samples show a wide range of sp. surface area and nitrogen content.  The sample activated at 600°C with the alkali/carbon ratio of 4 is rich in nitrogen and micropores (&lt;1 nm), exhibiting the highest CO2 uptake of 6.5 mmol g-1 and the largest specific capacitance of 351 F g-1 at 0.1 A g-1.  Moreover, the sample activated at 800°C with the alkali/carbon ratio of 5.5 retained 260 F g-1 at 30 A g-1 with a retention rate of 98% after 10 000 cycles (1 A g-1), indicating the excellent retention capability under high current densities and long cycle life.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqLoEbut1dXsrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXQLS_klgWLg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmtVejtLc%253D&amp;md5=dd4f30e22342dbfd5902676902665316</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref16"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref16'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">16</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit16" data-doi="10.1039/C5TA00727E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Luo, X.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene nanosheets, carbon nanotubes, graphite, and activated carbon as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Xu-Feng; Yang, Cheng-Hsien; Peng, You-Yu; Pu, Nen-Wen; Ger, Ming-Der; Hsieh, Chien-Te; Chang, Jeng-Kuei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">19</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">10320-10326</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. sodium-ion storage properties of graphene nanosheets, carbon nanotubes, mesocarbon microbeads, and activated carbon are investigated.  An irreversible oxidn. occurs for the activated carbon electrode during desodiation, limiting its use in sodium-ion batteries.  The mesocarbon microbead electrode shows a negligible capacity (∼2 mA-h/g), since the graphitic structure has a low surface area and is thus not capable of storing a sufficient amt. of Na+.  In contrast, the carbon nanotube and graphene nanosheet electrodes exhibit reversible capacities of 82 and 220 mA-h/g, resp., at a charge-discharge rate of 30 mA/g.  The high electro-adsorption/desorption area, large no. of Na+ entrance/exit sites, and a large d-spacing of graphene nanosheets contribute to their superior Na+ storage capacity.  At a high rate of 5 A/g, the graphene nanosheet electrode still delivers a capacity of as high as 105 mA-h/g, indicating great high-power ability.  The charge storage mechanism of the electrode is examd. using an ex situ x-ray diffraction technique.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGowDTJBbvo0n7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljXQLS_klgWLg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXmsFeks7k%253D&amp;md5=c2f6190841db243bc12579efa236802f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.05.084"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Huo, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">An, W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peng, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cheng, G.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mesoporous nitrogen-doped carbon hollow spheres as high-performance anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huo, Kaifu; An, Weili; Fu, Jijiang; Gao, Biao; Wang, Lei; Peng, Xiang; Cheng, Gary J.; Chu, Paul K.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">324</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">233-238</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped mesoporous carbon hollow spheres (N-MCHSs) were prepd. using mesoporous silica hollow spheres as template and dopamine as carbon precursor.  The N-MCHSs demonstrate high sp. surface area and vegetable sponge-like mesoporous shell with interconnected "carbon bridges", facilitating continuous electron transport and Li ion diffusion, and making the whole structure more stable.  The influence of N contents and N-bonding configuration on the Li storage of N-MCHSs is discussed.  The N-MCHSs carbonized at 800 °C demonstrate high reversible capacity and excellent rate performance, delivering a capacity of 485 mAh g-1 at a current of 0.5 A g-1 after 1,100 cycles.  Even up to 4.0 A g-1, a high capacity of 214 mAh g-1 can be remained.  The high electrochem. performance of N-MCHSs can be ascribed to mesoporous carbon hollow spheres structure and high level pyridinic nitrogen doping.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq44izzJ-hpF7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgaAoyhM4ttHw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XoslaksLs%253D&amp;md5=ce69db397339905d56e0de355f22cdb8</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1038/srep19317"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jin, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gao, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile Synthesis of Non-Graphitizable Polypyrrole-Derived Carbon/Carbon Nanotubes for Lithium-ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Jin, Bo; Gao, Fan; Zhu, Yong-Fu; Lang, Xing-You; Han, Gao-Feng; Gao, Wang; Wen, Zi; Zhao, Ming; Li, Jian-Chen; Jiang, Qing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite is usually used as an anode material in the com. lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  The relatively low lithium storage capacity of 372 mAh g-1 and the confined rate capability however limit its large-scale applications in elec. vehicles and hybrid elec. vehicles.  As results, exploring novel carbon-based anode materials with improved reversible capacity for high-energy-d. LIBs is urgent task.  Herein we present TNGC/MWCNTs by synthesizing tubular polypyrrole (T-PPy) via a self-assembly process, then carbonizing T-PPy at 900 °C under an argon atm. (TNGC for short) and finally mixing TNGC with multi-walled carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs).  As for TNGC/MWCNTs, the discharge capacity of 561 mAh g-1 is maintained after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  Electrochem. results demonstrate that TNGC/MWCNTs can be considered as promising anode materials for high-energy-d. LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqrd0KVMZQD_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgaAoyhM4ttHw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xos1KmtA%253D%253D&amp;md5=aec826cff782e5103a161a33eedd0c50</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2015.10.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanoribbons for High-Performance Gas Adsorbents and Lithium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yang, Quan-Sheng; Sui, Zhu-Yin; Liu, Yu-Wen; Han, Bao-Hang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Industrial &amp; Engineering Chemistry Research</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">22</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">6384-6390</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, we reported a novel and facile method for the fabrication of highly porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanoribbons (NCNs) by using KOH as an activating agent and polypyrrole nanoribbons as carbon and nitrogen precursors.  The as-prepd. NCNs exhibited an ultrahigh sp. surface area (2230 m2 g-1), large pore vol. (1.2 cm3 g-1), high nitrogen content (8.4 at %), and excellent thermal stability.  Given the above features, the NCNs as gas adsorbents possessed a high uptake capacity for carbon dioxide (24.5 wt %) and methane (3.0 wt %) at 1.0 bar and 273 K.  Furthermore, the NCNs as anode materials for lithium ion batteries delivered a high reversible capacity, good rate capacity, and excellent cycling performance due to the combined advantages of the high accessible porosity and enhanced electrochem. activity of doped nitrogen atoms.  Therefore, the highly porous NCNs may hold promise in the fields of energy and environment.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrX_d0lP6S477Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgaAoyhM4ttHw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XotFKrsb8%253D&amp;md5=082c87119c0dc246146e286e2107ce30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA00242K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peer, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pol, V.                         cas_cit21R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">21</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Long cycle life microporous spherical carbon anodes for sodium-ion batteries derived from furfuryl alcohol</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhou, Dehua; Peer, Maryam; Yang, Zhenzhen; Pol, Vilas G.; Key, Fulya Dogan; Jorne, Jacob; Foley, Henry C.; Johnson, Christopher S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

                        cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Biomass derived hard carbon used as a high performance anode material for sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hong, Kun-lei; Long, Qie; Zeng, Rui; Yi, Zi-qi; Zhang, Wei; Wang, Duo; Yin, Wei; Wu, Chao; Fan, Qing-jie; Zhang, Wu-xing; Huang, Yun-hui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The sodium storage mechanisms of the porous hard carbon can be explained by Na+ intercalation into the disordered graphene layers, redox reaction of the surface O-contg. functional groups and Na+ storage in the nanoscale pores.  However, the porous hard carbon demonstrated a low coulombic efficiency of 27%, resulting from the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase film and the side reactions of surface phosphorus groups.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoldD5kAMcszLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgaAoyhM4ttHw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVKmtbrO&amp;md5=9b28ca12b1ea3a55e7e2ada7ae1e05f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit23" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms6261"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Lithium Anodic Performance of Highly Nitrogen-doped Porous Carbon Prepared from a Metal-organic Framework</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.                         cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High lithium anodic performance of highly nitrogen-doped porous carbon prepared from a metal-organic framework</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zheng, Fangcai; Yang, Yang; Chen, Qianwang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Theor. and exptl. results have revealed that the lithium-ion storage capacity for nitrogen-doped graphene largely depends on the nitrogen-doping level.  However, most nitrogen-doped carbon materials used for lithium-ion batteries are reported to have a nitrogen content of approx. 10 wt% because a higher no. of nitrogen atoms in the two-dimensional honeycomb lattice can result in structural instability.  Here we report nitrogen-doped graphene particle analogs with a nitrogen content of up to 17.72 wt% that are prepd. by the pyrolysis of a nitrogen-contg. zeolitic imidazolate framework at 800 °C under a nitrogen atm.  As an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, these particles retain a capacity of 2,132 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, and 785 mAh g-1 after 1,000 cycles at 5 A g-1.  The remarkable performance results from the graphene analogous particles doped with nitrogen within the hexagonal lattice and edges.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqDx-A-uZG9bbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgM-E5LMLes2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFeisLvE&amp;md5=54792435037037c3dbd58dd2ece8d10e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref24"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref24'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">24</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit24" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2015.08.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Selvamani, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ravikumar, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Suryanarayanan, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Velayutham, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gopukumar, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Fish Scale Derived Nitrogen Doped Hierarchical Porous Carbon - a High Rate Performing Anode for Lithium Ion Cell</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Facile synthesis of microsized MnO/C composites with high tap density as high performance anodes for Li-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Jian-Gan; Liu, Huanyan; Liu, Hongzhen; Fu, Zihao; Nan, Ding</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Engineering Journal (Amsterdam, Netherlands)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">328</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">591-598</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Microsized MnO/C composites are synthesized through a facile strategy of in situ interfacial polymn. followed by a simple carbonization process.  The MnO/C composites exhibit solid microspherical structure having low sp. surface area and high tap d.  When evaluated as an anode material for Li-ion batteries, the MnO/C composites show a high gravimetric/volumetric specific capacity of 818 mAh g-1/1374 mAh cm-3 at 100 mA g-1, excellent cycling stability (a capacity retention rate of 99.3% after 100 cycles), and good rate capacity.  The microsized MnO/C anode also manifests outstanding capacity recoverability in the different cut-off voltage range of 1.5-3.0 V.  The excellent Li-ion storage properties of the MnO/C solid microspheres demonstrate its potential feasibility of practical application for high-performance Li-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoU-PucPXSHmLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgM-E5LMLes2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXht1Wls7fL&amp;md5=f68ac7fadbaa45fe75b5c20edbf5aec3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref27'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201100691"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">White, R.                         cas_cit28R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">28</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A honeycomb-like porous carbon derived from pomelo peel for use in high-performance supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liang, Qinghua; Ye, Ling; Huang, Zheng-Hong; Xu, Qiang; Bai, Yu; Kang, Feiyu; Yang, Quan-Hong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nanoscale</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A cost-effective approach to obtain electrode materials with excellent electrochem. performance is crit. to the development of supercapacitors (SCs).  Here we report the prepn. of a three-dimensional (3D) honeycomb-like porous carbon (HLPC) by the simple carbonization of pomelo peel followed by KOH activation.  Structural characterization indicates that the as-prepd. HLPC with a high sp. surface area (SSA) up to 2725 m2 g-1 is made up of interconnected microporous carbon walls.  Chem. anal. shows that the HLPC is doped with nitrogen and also has oxygen-contg. groups.  Electrochem. measurements show that the HLPC not only exhibits a high specific capacitance of 342 F g-1 and 171 F cm-3 at 0.2 A g-1 but also shows considerable rate capability with a retention of 62% at 20 A g-1 as well as good cycling performance with 98% retention over 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1 in 6 M KOH.  Furthermore, an as-fabricated HLPC-based sym. SC device delivers a max. energy d. of ∼9.4 Wh kg-1 in the KOH electrolyte.  Moreover, the outstanding cycling stability (only 2% capacitance decay over 1000 cycles at 5 A g-1) of the SC device makes it promising for use in a high-performance electrochem. energy system.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGomZMRVqMdGFbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgM-E5LMLes2g"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhsFCiur%252FL&amp;md5=2f95b4f295bcd15e0e4e9eafcaabcc17</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref29"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref29'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">29</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit29" data-doi="10.1039/c3ta14806h"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sun, Z.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Electrospun Carbon Nanofibers as Anode Materials for Sodium Ion Batteries with Excellent Cycle Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A simple and scalable electrospinning process followed by thermal treatment was used to fabricate carbon nanofibers.  The as-prepd. carbon nanofibers were investigated as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries.  Remarkably, due to their weakly ordered turbostratic structure and a large interlayer spacing between graphene sheets, the carbon nanofibers exhibit a dominant adsorption/insertion sodium storage mechanism that shows high reversibility. Reversible capacities of 233 and 82 mA-h/g are obtained for the carbon nanofibers at a c.d. of 0.05 A/g and even a high c.d. of 2 A/g, resp.                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical Porous Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanosheets Derived from Silk for Ultrahigh-Capacity Battery Anodes and Supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hou, Jianhua; Cao, Chuanbao; Idrees, Faryal; Ma, Xilan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">9</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2556-2564</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical porous N-doped C (HPNC) nanosheets (NS) have been prepd. via simultaneous activation and graphitization of biomass-derived natural silk.  The as-obtained HPNC-NS show favorable features for electrochem. energy storage such as high sp. surface area (SBET: 2494 m2/g), high vol. of hierarchical pores (2.28 cm3/g), nanosheet structures, rich N-doping (4.7%), and defects.  With respect to the multiple synergistic effects of these features, a Li-ion battery anode and a 2-electrode-based supercapacitor have been prepd.  A reversible Li storage capacity of 1865 mA-h/g was reported, which is the highest for N-doped C anode materials to the best of the knowledge.  The HPNC-NS supercapacitor's electrode in ionic liq. electrolytes exhibit a capacitance of 242 F/g and energy d. of 102 W-h/kg (48 W h/L), with high cycling life stability (9% loss after 10,000 cycles).  Thus, a high-performance Li-ion battery and supercapacitors were successfully assembled for the same electrode material, which was obtained through a 1-step and facile large-scale synthesis route.  It is promising for next-generation hybrid energy storage and renewable delivery devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr494WiQy0tj7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAZxuajgINdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXjtF2ru7w%253D&amp;md5=a11cbf1765f283e9955f033dc514d5fd</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2015.06.076"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ge, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jiang, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fu, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-doped Carbon Nanofibers Derived from Polyacrylonitrile for use as Anode Material in Sodium-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">94</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">189</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">195</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers derived from polyacrylonitrile for use as anode material in sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhu, Jiadeng; Chen, Chen; Lu, Yao; Ge, Yeqian; Jiang, Han; Fu, Kun; Zhang, Xiangwu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">94</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">189-195</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped carbon nanofibers (N-CNFs) derived from polyacrylonitrile were successfully synthesized by a combination of electrospinning and thermal treatment processes.  The as-prepd. N-CNFs were used as anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to their unique fabric and weakly-ordered turbostratic structure as well as large spacing between graphene layers.  Results show that N-CNFs carbonized at 800 °C delivered a high reversible capacity of 293 mAh/g at a c.d. of 50 mA/g in the first cycle.  Even though the first-cycle Coulombic efficiency was 64%, it increased to nearly 100% only after a few initial cycles.  Addnl., these N-CNFs showed excellent cycling and high-rate performance, and maintained a capacity of up to 150 mAh/g even at an extremely high c.d. of 1000 mA/g for over 200 cycles.  It is, therefore, demonstrated that N-CNFs prepd. under appropriate conditions are promising anode material candidate for sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqj55oWiOTyJ7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAZxuajgINdQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsVequ7nP&amp;md5=06248a7634670547df5ef87b30b304c6</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1038/srep39099"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Choi, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Seo, S.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhanced Lithium Storage in Hierarchically Porous Carbon Derived from Waste Tea Leaves</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Choi, Changhoon; Seo, Seung-Deok; Kim, Byung-Kook; Kim, Dong-Wan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Scientific Reports</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, highly nanoporous carbon (HCl-TW-Car) was successfully synthesized using a facile procedure combining acid treatment with a carbonization process that uses waste tea leaves from spent tea bags as raw materials.  The acid treatment not only promotes the efficient removal of unnecessary inorg. impurities but also increases the product porosity to enable synthesis of hierarchically porous carbon materials with various micro-, meso-, and macropores.  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, HCl-TW-Car demonstrated a much higher discharge capacity than is theor. possible using graphite [479 mAh g-1 after the 200th cycle at a rate of 0.2C (1C = 372 mA g-1)] and exhibited greater rate capabilities compared with those of carbonated products from tea waste without acid treatment.  It was shown that the good electrochem. properties of HCl-TW-Car can be ascribed to large Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area, well-formed hierarchical pores, and the prevention of unexpected electrochem. reactions from the redn. of metallic atoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq29778jABQQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhAZxuajgINdQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene-based nitrogen-doped carbon sandwich nanosheets: a new capacitive process controlled anode material for high-performance sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dongdong; Zhang, Lei; Chen, Hongbin; Wang, Jun; Ding, Liang-Xin; Wang, Suqing; Ashman, Peter J.; Wang, Haihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode materials with capacitive charge storage (CCS) are highly desirable for the development of high-performance Na-ion batteries (SIBs), because the capacitive process usually shows kinetically high ion diffusion and superior structural stability.  Here, the authors report a new CCS anode material of graphene-based N-doped C sandwich nanosheets (G-NCs).  The as-prepd. G-NCs show a high capacitive contribution during the discharge/charge processes.                         cas_cit36R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">36</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped carbon/graphene hybrid anode material for sodium-ion batteries with excellent rate capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Huan; Jia, Mengqiu; Cao, Bin; Chen, Renjie; Lv, Xinying; Tang, Renjie; Wu, Feng; Xu, Bin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

The NCG has a large interlayer distance (0.360 nm) and a high nitrogen content of 7.54 at%, resulting in a high reversible sodium storage capacity of 336 mAh/g at 30 mA/g. Mater. Chem.                 10.1039/C5TA09066K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D4%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D1423-1431%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DX.%2BLiu%26author%3DJ.%2BZhang%26author%3DS.%2BGuo%26author%3DN.%2BPinna%26title%3DGraphene%252FN-doped%2BCarbon%2BSandwiched%2BNanosheets%2Bwith%2BUltrahigh%2BNitrogen%2BDoping%2Bfor%2BBoosting%2BLithium-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC5TA09066K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10882&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC5TA09066K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit37R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">37</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Graphene/N-doped carbon sandwiched nanosheets with ultrahigh nitrogen doping for boosting lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Liu, Xianghong; Zhang, Jun; Guo, Shaojun; Pinna, Nicola</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">4</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1423-1431</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Enhancing the nitrogen (N) doping in carbon nanomaterials has been suggested as an effective approach to enhance the performance of lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, achieving N-doped carbon nanomaterials with an ultrahigh N content is still a great challenge, thus limiting the capacity enhancement.  Herein, we demonstrate a new procedure for the synthesis of unique sandwich architecture of N-doped carbon/reduced graphene oxide (N-carbon/rGO) derived from simple pyrolysis of a polypyrrole/GO nanosheet precursor.  The N-carbon/rGO exhibits the highest N-doping of 15.4% reported in all the carbon-based nanomaterials, and a high sp. surface area of 327 m2 g-1 with a micro/mesoporous structure.  They combine the advantages of high cond. of rGO, very high N-functionalities, and the porous structure of carbons, which endow them with appealing electrochem. lithium storage properties with a high initial reversible capacity of 1100 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, excellent rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and superior cycling stability over 1000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1.  The present work highlights the important role of tuning the nitrogen doping in enhancing the performance of LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCjCHAlSOj3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhkg4mCB-zJDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XnsF2mtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=60b41095b6fdbbb830bae62cfc93f035</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref38'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.08.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium and Sodium Storage in Highly Ordered Mesoporous Nitrogen-doped Carbons Derived from Honey</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.
