                10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.08.096</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D335%26publication_year%3D2016%26pages%3D20-30%26journal%3DJ.%2BPower%2BSources%26author%3DY.%2BZhang%26author%3DL.%2BChen%26author%3DY.%2BMeng%26author%3DJ.%2BXie%26author%3DY.%2BGuo%26author%3DD.%2BXiao%26title%3DLithium%2Band%2BSodium%2BStorage%2Bin%2BHighly%2BOrdered%2BMesoporous%2BNitrogen-doped%2BCarbons%2BDerived%2Bfrom%2BHoney%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.jpowsour.2016.08.096&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10882&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.jpowsour.2016.08.096&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium and sodium storage in highly ordered mesoporous nitrogen-doped carbons derived from honey</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Yongzhi; Chen, Li; Meng, Yan; Xie, Jun; Guo, Yong; Xiao, Dan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">335</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">20-30</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Honey, a widely existent biomass, consists mainly of carbohydrate and other N-contg. substances such as proteins, enzymes and org. acids.  It can be mixed homogeneously with mesoporous SiO2 template for its excellent H2O-soly. and moderate viscosity.  Honey was employed as a N-contg. C precursor to prep. N-doped ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs).  The obtained honey derived mesoporous N-doped carbons (HMNCs) with dilated interlayer spacings of 0.387-0.395 nm, narrow pore size distributions centering at ∼4 nm and satisfactory N contents of 1.38-4.32% offer superb dual functionality for Li-ion battery (LIB) and Na-ion battery (NIB) anodes.  Tested against Li, the optimized HMNC-700 delivers a superior reversible capacity of 1359 mA h g-1 after 10 cycles at 100 mA g-1 and excellent rate capability and cycling stability of 722 mA h g-1 after 200 cycles at 1 A g-1.  For NIB applications, HMNC-700 offers a high initial reversible capacity of 427 mA h g-1 and stable reversible capacity of 394 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqvNRB77GZElLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhkg4mCB-zJDQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Preparation of renewable lignin-derived nitrogen-doped carbon nanospheres as anodes for lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Huajun; Wang, Qiujun; Deng, Yonghong; Shi, Qiao; Qian, Yong; Wang, Bingbing; Lu, Lei; Qiu, Xueqing</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">RSC Advances</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">6</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">81</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">77143-77150</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">RSCACL</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2046-2069</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">For the common concern that general lignin-based colloidal spheres suffer the weakness of spherical structure destruction during the pyrolysis process, novel uniform lignin-derived nitrogen-doped carbon nanospheres were prepd. by direct pyrolysis of lignin-based azo polymer (AL-azo-NO2) colloidal spheres at 750 °C.  In addn., a kind of hard carbon with high graphitization degree was also prepd. as a control by direct pyrolysis of alkali lignin (AL).  The morphol. and structure of the as-obtained carbon materials were investigated by field emission SEM, X-ray diffraction patterns, Raman spectra and elemental anal.  They served as anodes in lithium-ion batteries with the aim to investigate the electrochem. performance.  These two kinds of lignin-derived carbon materials exhibited different electrochem. performances due to their various structures and functional groups.  The nitrogen-doped carbon nanospheres (CSAN-750) exhibited a high cyclic stable capacity up to 225 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 60 mA g-1 after 50 cycles (CAL-750, 120 mA h g-1) coupled with high first coulombic efficiency up to 66.4% for CSAN-3000 with a cyclic capacity of 200 mA h g-1, which is more comparable to that of the CAL-3000 (53.3%, 199 mA h g-1).  This research indicates the great promise of lignin applied in producing hard carbon materials and further energy storage systems.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoohPbe0l6CCbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhkg4mCB-zJDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xht12nurrI&amp;md5=32fb63c0027df66d37dd1698472edfa3</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1016/j.micromeso.2017.03.019"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mondal, A.                 10.1016/j.micromeso.2017.03.019</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D246%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D72-80%26journal%3DMicroporous%2BMesoporous%2BMater.%26author%3DA.%2BK.%2BMondal%26author%3DK.%2BKretschmer%26author%3DY.%2BZhao%26author%3DH.%2BLiu%26author%3DH.%2BFan%26author%3DG.%2BWang%26title%3DNaturally%2BNitrogen%2BDoped%2BPorous%2BCarbon%2Bderived%2Bfrom%2BWaste%2BShrimp%2BShells%2Bfor%2BHigh-performance%2BLithium%2BIon%2BBatteries%2Band%2BSupercapacitors%26doi%3D10.1016%252Fj.micromeso.2017.03.019&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10882&amp;doiOfLink=10.1016%2Fj.micromeso.2017.03.019&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Naturally nitrogen doped porous carbon derived from waste shrimp shells for high-performance lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mondal, Anjon Kumar; Kretschmer, Katja; Zhao, Yufei; Liu, Hao; Fan, Hongbo; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Microporous and Mesoporous Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">246</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">72-80</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">MIMMFJ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1387-1811</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transformation of biomass wastes into sustainable low cost carbon materials is now a topic of great interest.  Here, we describe porous carbon from biomass derived waste shrimp shells and its application in two different energy storage systems.  The unique porous structure with the presence of heteroatoms (O, N) makes it promising material for both lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors.  When applied as anode materials for lithium ion batteries, the as-prepd. carbon showed a specific capacity as high as 1507 mA h g-1 and 1014 mA h g-1 at current densities of 0.1 A g-1 and 0.5 A g-1, resp., good rate performance and superior cycling stability.  The porous carbon-based supercapacitor also delivered a specific capacitance of 239 F g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 in 6 M KOH electrolyte.  The specific capacitance retention is 99.4% even after 5000 charge-discharge cycles, indicating excellent cycling stability.  The superior electrochem. performances for both lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors could be ascribed to the high sp. surface area, porous structure and nitrogen doping effect.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBw8_YqwycCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhkg4mCB-zJDQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFymtbg%253D&amp;md5=a971ce97ed34a34dfb54e38000bbc80a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref41'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s13391-017-6223-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xi, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nitrogen Doped Carbon Derived from Horn Comb as Anode for Sodium-ion Storage with High Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electron.                         cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Hierarchical porous nitrogen doped carbon derived from horn comb as anode for sodium-ion storage with high performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ou, Junke; Yang, Lin; Xi, Xianghui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electronic Materials Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">66-71</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EMLLAE</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1738-8090</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Springer</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Horn comb, an abundant biomass waste, has been successfully converted into a hierarchical porous nitrogen doped carbon (HPNDC) via a simple and cost-effective approach.  Tested as anode for sodium ion batteries (SIBs), horn comb derived carbon shows good rate capability and cycling stability, delivering a high initial charge capacity of 400 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, retaining a reversible capacity of 112 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1, and exhibiting a capacity of 241 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 after 100 cycles.  These superior electrochem. performances can be ascribed to its unique hierarchical pore structure combined with appropriate nitrogen doping effects.  We believe that our works will be helpful in promoting the development of high-rate and low-cost sodium ion batteries for large-scale energy storage systems.                         cas_cit42R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">42</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-doped porous carbon nanoparticle derived from nitrogen containing conjugated microporous polymer as high performance lithium battery anode</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Qingtang; Dai, Qinqin; Yan, Chao; Su, Ce; Li, An</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Alloys and Compounds</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">714</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">204-212</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped porous C nanoparticle (NPCN) was obtained by pyrolyzing N-contg. conjugated microporous polymer (NCMP).  KOH high temp. activation following HNO3 neutralizing was also used to acquire NPCN-KOH with improved porous structure.  NPCN and NPCN-KOH were characterized by SEM, TEM, XPS, Raman spectroscopy, BET, cyclic voltammetry and charge-discharge test.  SEM results indicate that both NPCN and NPCN-KOH are nanoparticles with a size ∼100 nm.  TEM results imply that KOH activation promotes the catalyst granules fusing together to form large particles in NPCN-KOH.  XPS and elemental anal. indicate HNO3 neutralizing can increase the N content.  Raman spectroscopy indicate NPCN-KOH possess more disordered structure.  BET anal. reveals that sp. surface area of NPCN-KOH is 1845 m2/g, which is much larger than that of NPCN.  These unique features ensure NPCN-KOH exhibit high reversible capacity, large rate performance and long cycling life.  NPCN-KOH delivers a reversible capacity of 818 mAh/g.  The capacity of NPCN-KOH cycled at 1 C for 600 cycles is as high as 527 mAh/g, with a capacity retention ratio of 97.6%.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpdkeaKH-Xg-bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQY1o4iFz70Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXmsl2qsLo%253D&amp;md5=05e357a763bf285db71085c6318aa9cf</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref43"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref43'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">43</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit43" data-doi="10.1016/j.carbon.2017.02.057"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, G.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lu, T.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pan, L.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Covalent-organic-frameworks Derived N-doped Porous Carbon materials as Anode for Superior Long-life Cycling Lithium and Sodium Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Carbon</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">116</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">686</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">694</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit43R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">43</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Covalent-organic-frameworks derived N-doped porous carbon materials as anode for superior long-life cycling lithium and sodium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhang, Xiaojie; Zhu, Guang; Wang, Miao; Li, Jiabao; Lu, Ting; Pan, Likun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">116</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">686-694</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CRBNAH</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped porous carbon materials (NPCs) were prepd. by the carbonization of covalent-org. frameworks as precursors and used as anodes for lithium and sodium ion batteries (LIBs and SIBs) for the first time.  The morphol., structure, and electrochem. performance were characterized and evaluated by field emission SEM, transmission electron microscopy, XPS, Raman spectroscopy, X-ray diffraction, nitrogen adsorption and desorption isotherms, galvanostatic charge/discharge tests, cyclic voltammetry, and electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, resp.  The NPCs not only show high max. reversible charge capacities of 488 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1 (LIBs) and 237.7 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1 (SIBs) after 100 cycles, but also deliver high reversible charge capacities of 143 mAh g-1 at 5 A g-1 (LIBs) and 88.8 mAh g-1 at 2.5 A g-1 (SIBs) and excellent rate performance.  Moreover, superior long-life cycling stability is obsd. for 5000 cycles even at a very high c.d. of 5 A g-1 for LIBs and 2.5 A g-1 for SIBs.  The excellent electrochem. performance of NPCs with superior reversible capacity, good rate performance, and long-life cycling stability is attributed to their N doping, high sp. surface area and porous structure with large interlayer distance.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpdGsdDWlmTJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQY1o4iFz70Q"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Porous nitrogen doped carbon sphere as high performance anode of sodium-ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Dongdong; Chen, Hongbin; Liu, Guoxue; Wei, Meng; Ding, Liang-xin; Wang, Suqing; Wang, Haihui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Carbon</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">94</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The carbon material is regarded as the most promising anode candidate for sodium ion battery.  In this paper, we found that the porous structure is a crit. factor for the improving of carbon anode material.  Porous structure is successfully fabricated in nitrogen doped carbon sphere (N-CS) via the mature template-assisted method and the sodium storage property of the porous nitrogen doped carbon sphere (P-N-CS) and N-CS is investigated.  The results show that the P-N-CS possesses super rate capability of 155 mA h g-1 at 1 A g-1, which is much higher than that of N-CS (18 mA h g-1).  In addn., the P-N-CS exhibits outstanding cycle stability with 206 mA h g-1 after 600 cycles at 0.2 A g-1 and the capacity of N-CS is only 96 mA h g-1 at the same condition.  The super electrochem. performance of P-N-CS could be attributed to the high content of pores.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Garlic peel derived high capacity hierarchical N-doped porous carbon anode for sodium/lithium ion cell</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Selvamani, V.; Ravikumar, R.; Suryanarayanan, V.; Velayutham, D.; Gopukumar, S.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Electrochimica Acta</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">N-doped porous C synthesized from garlic peel by a simple and cost-effective method was employed as an anode material for the Na ion (SIB) as well as Li ion batteries (LIB).  The synthesized material is mesoporous with a high sp. surface area (SSA) ∼1710 m2 g-1, as calcd. with Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) isotherm.  Further, Field Emission SEM (FE-SEM) and TEM anal. reveal the existence of interconnected micro-pores and voids.  The N-doped garlic peel C (GPC) exhibits excellent rate capability as well as steady state cycling performance towards Na and Li ion shuttlings.  Discharge capacities of ∼142, 89, 58, 37 mAh g-1 were achieved at various current densities such as 0.5, 1.0, 2.0, 4.0 A g-1 resp. in a CR-2032 type Na-ion cell.  Similarly, the Li-ion cell delivered reversible capacities of ∼320, 280, 215 and 145 mAh g-1 at different current densities of 1.0, 2.0, 4.0 and 8.0 A g-1, resp.  The high electrochem. performance of the N-doped GPC is mainly attributed to the existence of N in the C matrix and mesoporous structure coupled with a high surface area for accommodating large no. of Li/Na ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGojS4zcKmFSt7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljQY1o4iFz70Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XoslSksg%253D%253D&amp;md5=5dc465fb9a1215bb8fa8e99048e2d86d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.1039/C6NJ04026H"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Selvamani, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Suryanarayanan, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Velayutham, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gopukumar, S.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Lithium Anodic Performance of N-doped Porous Biocarbon-integrated Indium Sulfide Thin Nanosheets</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">New J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A triazine-based porous carbon material (TPC-1) was prepd. directly from a fluorinated arom. nitrile in molten zinc chloride.  Trimerization of the nitrile and subsequent defluorination carbonization of the polymeric network gave TPC-1.  The defluorination process is reversible and can etch the polymeric network to release CFn, thereby generating addnl. porosity and rendering TPC-1 a nitrogen-rich porous material.  TPC-1 shows a high BET surface area of 1940 m2 g-1 and contains both micropores and mesopores, which facilitate the diffusion and adsorption of gas mols.                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lithium Charge Storage Mechanisms of Cross-Linked Triazine Networks and Their Porous Carbon Derivatives</span></div><div class="casAuthors">See, Kimberly A.; Hug, Stephan; Schwinghammer, Katharina; Lumley, Margaret A.; Zheng, Yonghao; Nolt, Jaya M.; Stucky, Galen D.; Wudl, Fred; Lotsch, Bettina V.; Seshadri, Ram</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox active electrode materials derived from org. precursors are of interest for use as alternative cathodes in Li batteries due to the potential for their sustainable prodn. from renewable resources.  Here, a series of org. networks that either contain triazine units or are derived from triazine-contg. precursors are evaluated as cathodes vs. Li metal anodes as possible active materials in Li batteries.  The role of the mol. structure on the electrochem. performance is studied by comparing several materials prepd. across a range of conditions allowing control over functionality and long-range order.  Well-defined structures in which the triazine unit persists in the final material exhibit very low capacities at voltages relevant for cathode materials (&lt; 10 mA·h g-1).  Relatively high, reversible capacity (around 150 mA·h g-1) is in fact displayed by amorphous materials with little evidence of triazine functionality.  This result directly contradicts previous suggestions that the triazine unit is responsible for charge storage in this family of materials.  While the gently sloping discharge and charge profiles suggest a capacitive-type mechanism-further confirmed by the trend of increasing capacity with increasing surface area-ESR (EPR) spectroscopy studies show that the materials exhibiting higher capacities also display substantial EPR signals, potentially implicating unpaired spins in a charge storage mechanism that could involve charge transfer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLLZ7ezje3ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgN8k5hltW6Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXosFGntLk%253D&amp;md5=90dd8be697055066bd4e67619ae6eb20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE02574E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Schwinghammer, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hug, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mesch, M.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Phenyl-triazine oligomers for light-driven hydrogen evolution</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Schwinghammer, K.; Hug, S.; Mesch, M. B.; Senker, J.; Lotsch, B. V.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Energy &amp; Environmental Science</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3345-3353</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EESNBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1754-5706</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of stable, yet highly tunable org. photocatalysts which orchestrate multi-step electron transfer reactions is at the heart of the newly emerging field of polymer photocatalysis.  Covalent triazine frameworks such as the archetypal CTF-1 have been theorized to constitute a new class of photocatalytically active polymers for light-driven water splitting.  Here, we revisit the ionothermal synthesis of CTF-1 by trimerization of 1,4-dicyanobenzene catalyzed by the Lewis acid zinc chloride and demonstrate that the microporous black polymer CTF-1 is essentially inactive for hydrogen evolution.  Instead, highly photoactive phenyl-triazine oligomers (PTOs) with higher crystallinity as compared to CTF-1 are obtained by lowering the reaction temp. to 300 °C and prolonging the reaction time to &gt;150 h.  The low reaction temp. of the PTOs largely prevents incipient carbonization and thus results in a carbon-to-nitrogen wt. ratio close to the theor. value of 3.43.  The oligomers were characterized by MALDI-TOF and quant. solid-state NMR spectroscopy, revealing variations in size, connectivity and thus nitrile-to-triazine ratios depending on the initial precursor diln.  The most active PTO samples efficiently and stably reduce water to hydrogen with an av. rate of 1076 (±278) μmol h-1 g-1 under simulated sunlight illumination, which is competitive with the best carbon nitride-based and purely org. photocatalysts.  The photocatalytic activity of the PTOs is found to sensitively depend on the polymn. degree, thus suggesting a prominent role of the unreacted nitrile moieties in the photocatalytic process.  Notably, PTOs even show moderate hydrogen prodn. without the addn. of any co-catalyst.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGox92N4Z0ZAJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgN8k5hltW6Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2lt7nL&amp;md5=ef3692a27182894f48c1c31f87990a2e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/la403366e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhattacharjya, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, H.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nitrogen-Doped Carbon Nanoparticles by Flame Synthesis as Anode Material for Rechargeable Lithium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bhattacharjya, Dhrubajyoti; Park, Hyean-Yeol; Kim, Min-Sik; Choi, Hyuck-Soo; Inamdar, Shaukatali N.; Yu, Jong-Sung</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Langmuir</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped turbostratic carbon nanoparticles (NPs) are prepd. using fast single-step flame synthesis by directly burning acetonitrile in air atm. and investigated as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries.  The as-prepd. N-doped carbon NPs show excellent Li-ion storage properties with initial discharge capacity of 596 mA.h.g-1, which is 17% more than that shown by the corresponding undoped carbon NPs synthesized by identical process with acetone as carbon precursor and also much higher than that of com. graphite anode.  Further anal. shows that the charge-discharge process of N-doped carbon is highly stable and reversible not only at high c.d. but also over 100 cycles, retaining 71% of initial discharge capacity.  Electrochem. impedance spectroscopy also shows that N-doped carbon has better cond. for charge and ions than that of undoped carbon.  The high specific capacity and very stable cyclic performance are attributed to large no. of turbostratic defects and N and assocd. increased O content in the flame-synthesized N-doped carbon.  To the best of our knowledge, this is the first report which demonstrates single-step, direct flame synthesis of N-doped turbostratic carbon NPs and their application as a potential anode material with high capacity and superior battery performance.  The method is extremely simple, low cost, energy efficient, very effective, and can be easily scaled up for large scale prodn.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoKzJ9aFjbqFrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgN8k5hltW6Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXhvFCisr3F&amp;md5=6367991dd1474c017236bc60dcb41b25</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b01969"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Surta, T. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dolgos, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">New Mechanistic Insights on Na-Ion Storage in Nongraphitizable Carbon</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nano Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2015</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">15</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">5888</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">5892</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acs.nanolett.5b01969</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D15%26publication_year%3D2015%26pages%3D5888-5892%26journal%3DNano%2BLett.%26author%3DC.%2BBommier%26author%3DT.%2BW.%2BSurta%26author%3DM.%2BDolgos%26author%3DX.%2BJi%26title%3DNew%2BMechanistic%2BInsights%2Bon%2BNa-Ion%2BStorage%2Bin%2BNongraphitizable%2BCarbon%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facs.nanolett.5b01969&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10882&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facs.nanolett.5b01969&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit53R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">53</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">New Mechanistic Insights on Na-Ion Storage in Nongraphitizable Carbon</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bommier, Clement; Surta, Todd Wesley; Dolgos, Michelle; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">5888-5892</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NALEFD</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1530-6984</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nongraphitizable carbon, also known as hard carbon, is considered one of the most promising anodes for the emerging Na-ion batteries.  The current mechanistic understanding of Na-ion storage in hard carbon is based on the "card-house" model first raised in the early 2000s.  This model describes that Na-ion insertion occurs first through intercalation between graphene sheets in turbostratic nanodomains, followed by Na filling of the pores in the carbon structure.  We tried to test this model by tuning the sizes of turbostratic nanodomains but revealed a correlation between the structural defects and Na-ion storage.  Based on our exptl. data, we propose an alternative perspective for sodiation of hard carbon that consists of Na-ion storage at defect sites, by intercalation and last via pore-filling.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqegbEbsDPzrrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgN8k5hltW6Jw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXht1Oqsb3M&amp;md5=a2144d9fa8c9f19a479ebec0ec74f1eb</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref54'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201602894"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bommier, C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Sen Chong, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jian, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Surta, T. W.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xing, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Neuefeind, J. C.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Stickle, W. F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Dolgos, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Greaney, P. A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ji, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Novel and Generalized Lithium-Ion-Battery Configuration utilizing Al Foil as Both Anode and Current Collector for Enhanced Energy Density</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                             cas_R
                        "><div class="casContent">There is no corresponding record for this reference.</div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref55"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">55</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit55" data-doi="10.1149/2.0041410eel"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Rashid, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gupta, A.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Mathematical Model for Combined Effect of SEI Formation and Gas Evolution in Li-ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">ECS Electrochem. Lett.</span><span class="NLM_x"> </span><span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_volume">3</span><span class="NLM_x">, </span> <span class="NLM_fpage">A95</span><span class="NLM_x">–</span> <span class="NLM_lpage">A98</span><span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1149/2.0041410eel</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D3%26publication_year%3D2014%26pages%3DA95-A98%26journal%3DECS%2BElectrochem.%2BLett.%26author%3DM.%2BRashid%26author%3DA.%2BGupta%26title%3DMathematical%2BModel%2Bfor%2BCombined%2BEffect%2Bof%2BSEI%2BFormation%2Band%2BGas%2BEvolution%2Bin%2BLi-ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1149%252F2.0041410eel&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.7b10882&amp;doiOfLink=10.1149%2F2.0041410eel&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit55R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">55</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Mathematical Model for Combined Effect of SEI Formation and Gas Evolution in Li-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rashid, Muhammad; Gupta, Amit</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ECS Electrochemistry Letters</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">10</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">A95-A98</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">EELCBY</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2162-8726</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Electrochemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, a math. model to investigate the combined effect of SEI film formation and gas evolution over the degrdn. of Li-ion cells is developed.  A Li-ion cell is simulated for three discharge/charge rates until 80% of the rated capacity is irreversibly lost in side reactions.  The model shows that the thickness of SEI film and vol. of gases evolved is between 0.03-0.22 μm and 1.6-10.6%, resp.  It is shown that, in addn. to greater diffusion limitations, capacity degrdn. at higher cycling rates is faster due to redn. in cyclable lithium caused by its accumulation in the neg. electrode.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrC2jC5Tdt3HrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljdahaPneCmwQ"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">First-principles calcns. were done to examine the energetics of alkali metal intercalation into graphite.  Calcns. based on the exchange-correlation functionals that include a nonlocal correlation were found to give reasonable agreement with expts. concerning the crystal structure of graphite and LiC6, binding energy of graphene sheets, and Li intercalation potential.  We found that K intercalation from KC8 to KC6 cannot be achieved through electrochem. reactions.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nanoscale porous C fibers (CNFs) were obtained by pyrolysis in an Ar atm. of a conducting polymer synthesized by a self-degrdn. template method.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The sodium storage mechanisms of the porous hard carbon can be explained by Na+ intercalation into the disordered graphene layers, redox reaction of the surface O-contg. functional groups and Na+ storage in the nanoscale pores.  However, the porous hard carbon demonstrated a low coulombic efficiency of 27%, resulting from the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase film and the side reactions of surface phosphorus groups.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoldD5kAMcszLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVBJJHRJrt5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVKmtbrO&amp;md5=9b28ca12b1ea3a55e7e2ada7ae1e05f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref12" class="rightTabRefNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit12" data-doi="10.1016/j.electacta.2014.09.052"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Suryawanshi, A.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mhamane, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Nagane, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Patil, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Aravindan, V.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ogale, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Srinivasan, M.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Indanthrone Derived Disordered Graphitic Carbon as Promising Insertion Anode for Sodium Ion Battery with Long Cycle life</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electrochim.                         rightTab-cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Electrospinning with partially carbonization in air: Highly porous carbon nanofibers optimized for high-performance flexible lithium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Weihan; Li, Minsi; Wang, Min; Zeng, Linchao; Yu, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Self-supported and flexible highly porous carbon nanofibers (HPCNFs) were prepd. by electrospinning method combined with a post-two-step carbonization process.  By introduction of air into the Ar flow during carbonization, carbon nanofibers were partially burnt off and a large no. of micro/mesopores were created.  As effective lithium storage units, the porous structure plays an important role in enhancing the electrochem. performances.  The HPCNFs delivers a reversible capacity as high as 1780 mAh g-1 after 40 cycles at 50 mA g-1 and ultralong cycle life (1550 mAh g-1 after 600 cycles at 500 mA g-1).  Even cycled at 25 A g-1, it still displays a very high capacity of 200 mAh g-1.  The outstanding electrochem. and mech. properties of HPCNFs are attributed to the novel structure: pores provide good access of the electrolyte to the electrode surface and facilitate fast charge transfer across the electrode/electrolyte interface. 3D interconnected networks decrease the contact resistance and improve elec. cond. of the overall electrode, which enhance electron transport rate.  Therefore, this novel carbon material holds great promise for potential applications in energy-related technol. and flexible electrodes for next generation LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNd91PVUFXXbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVBJJHRJrt5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXlslyrs74%253D&amp;md5=0d28e55b2245e971c28e1a64eaf647e0</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref14" class="rightTabRefNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit14" data-doi="10.1039/C4TA05451B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are expected to be a promising com. alternative to lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) for large-scale and low-cost elec. energy storage applications in the near future.  Despite this, the absence of a suitable neg. electrode material hinders their development.  In this contribution, the authors synthesized monodispersed hard carbon spherules (HCS) from an abundant biomass of sucrose, and studied the influence of the carbonization temp. on the microstructure and electrochem. performance.  The initial coulombic efficiency of the HCS was increased to 83% by coating its surface with soft carbon through the pyrolysis of toluene.  The plateau capacity at the low potential region increased with increasing carbonization temp.  The HCS carbonized at 1600° showed the highest plateau capacity (220 mA-h/g) and excellent cycling performance with a capacity retention of 93% after 100 cycles.  When coupled with an air-stable P2-Na2/3Ni1/3Mn2/3O2 pos. electrode, the full cell exhibited a high initial coulombic efficiency of 76%, a mean operating voltage of 3.5 V and excellent cycling performance.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A low cost carbon precursor to produce carbon with large sp. surface area and abundant heteroatoms is essential for CO2 uptake and supercapacitors to realize economic viability.  We report a facile synthesis method and superior performance of a kind of porous activated carbon based on chicken feather.  Herein, different activated temps. and alkali/carbon ratios (KOH vs. carbon in g/g) are used to tailor the pore structure and the surface chem., so the samples show a wide range of sp. surface area and nitrogen content.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. sodium-ion storage properties of graphene nanosheets, carbon nanotubes, mesocarbon microbeads, and activated carbon are investigated.  An irreversible oxidn. occurs for the activated carbon electrode during desodiation, limiting its use in sodium-ion batteries.  The mesocarbon microbead electrode shows a negligible capacity (∼2 mA-h/g), since the graphitic structure has a low surface area and is thus not capable of storing a sufficient amt. of Na+.  In contrast, the carbon nanotube and graphene nanosheet electrodes exhibit reversible capacities of 82 and 220 mA-h/g, resp., at a charge-discharge rate of 30 mA/g.  The high electro-adsorption/desorption area, large no. of Na+ entrance/exit sites, and a large d-spacing of graphene nanosheets contribute to their superior Na+ storage capacity.  At a high rate of 5 A/g, the graphene nanosheet electrode still delivers a capacity of as high as 105 mA-h/g, indicating great high-power ability.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite is usually used as an anode material in the com. lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  The relatively low lithium storage capacity of 372 mAh g-1 and the confined rate capability however limit its large-scale applications in elec. vehicles and hybrid elec. vehicles.  As results, exploring novel carbon-based anode materials with improved reversible capacity for high-energy-d. LIBs is urgent task.  Herein we present TNGC/MWCNTs by synthesizing tubular polypyrrole (T-PPy) via a self-assembly process, then carbonizing T-PPy at 900 °C under an argon atm. (TNGC for short) and finally mixing TNGC with multi-walled carbon nanotubes (MWCNTs).  As for TNGC/MWCNTs, the discharge capacity of 561 mAh g-1 is maintained after 100 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  Electrochem. results demonstrate that TNGC/MWCNTs can be considered as promising anode materials for high-energy-d. LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqrd0KVMZQD_rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhVBJJHRJrt5Q"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28Xos1KmtA%253D%253D&amp;md5=aec826cff782e5103a161a33eedd0c50</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref19" class="rightTabRefNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit19" data-doi="10.1016/j.ensm.2015.10.003"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Li, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hu, Y.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, we reported a novel and facile method for the fabrication of highly porous nitrogen-doped carbon nanoribbons (NCNs) by using KOH as an activating agent and polypyrrole nanoribbons as carbon and nitrogen precursors.  The as-prepd. NCNs exhibited an ultrahigh sp. surface area (2230 m2 g-1), large pore vol. (1.2 cm3 g-1), high nitrogen content (8.4 at %), and excellent thermal stability.  Given the above features, the NCNs as gas adsorbents possessed a high uptake capacity for carbon dioxide (24.5 wt %) and methane (3.0 wt %) at 1.0 bar and 273 K.  Furthermore, the NCNs as anode materials for lithium ion batteries delivered a high reversible capacity, good rate capacity, and excellent cycling performance due to the combined advantages of the high accessible porosity and enhanced electrochem. activity of doped nitrogen atoms.  Therefore, the highly porous NCNs may hold promise in the fields of energy and environment.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrX_d0lP6S477Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lieU-x57FO_oA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XotFKrsb8%253D&amp;md5=082c87119c0dc246146e286e2107ce30</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref21"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref21" class="rightTabRefNumLink">21</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit21" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA00242K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Peer, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Z.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Pol, V.             (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A porous hard carbon material was synthesized by the simple pyrolysis of H3PO4-treated biomass, i.e., pomelo peels, at 700 °C in N2.  The as-obtained hard carbon had a 3D connected porous structure and a large sp. surface area of 1272 m2 g-1.  XPS anal. showed that the carbon material was functionalized by O-contg. and P-contg. groups.  The porous hard carbon was used as an anode for sodium ion batteries and exhibited good cycling stability and rate capability, delivering a capacity of 181 mA h g-1 at 200 mA g-1 after 220 cycles and retaining a capacity of 71 mA h g-1 at 5 A g-1.  The sodium storage mechanisms of the porous hard carbon can be explained by Na+ intercalation into the disordered graphene layers, redox reaction of the surface O-contg. functional groups and Na+ storage in the nanoscale pores.  However, the porous hard carbon demonstrated a low coulombic efficiency of 27%, resulting from the formation of a solid electrolyte interphase film and the side reactions of surface phosphorus groups.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoldD5kAMcszLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lieU-x57FO_oA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhtVKmtbrO&amp;md5=9b28ca12b1ea3a55e7e2ada7ae1e05f9</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref23"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref23" class="rightTabRefNumLink">23</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit23" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms6261"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zheng, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, Q.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High Lithium Anodic Performance of Highly Nitrogen-doped Porous Carbon Prepared from a Metal-organic Framework</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Nat.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Theor. and exptl. results have revealed that the lithium-ion storage capacity for nitrogen-doped graphene largely depends on the nitrogen-doping level.  However, most nitrogen-doped carbon materials used for lithium-ion batteries are reported to have a nitrogen content of approx. 10 wt% because a higher no. of nitrogen atoms in the two-dimensional honeycomb lattice can result in structural instability.  Here we report nitrogen-doped graphene particle analogs with a nitrogen content of up to 17.72 wt% that are prepd. by the pyrolysis of a nitrogen-contg. zeolitic imidazolate framework at 800 °C under a nitrogen atm.  As an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, these particles retain a capacity of 2,132 mA h g-1 after 50 cycles at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1, and 785 mAh g-1 after 1,000 cycles at 5 A g-1.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A cost-effective approach to obtain electrode materials with excellent electrochem. performance is crit. to the development of supercapacitors (SCs).  Here we report the prepn. of a three-dimensional (3D) honeycomb-like porous carbon (HLPC) by the simple carbonization of pomelo peel followed by KOH activation.  Structural characterization indicates that the as-prepd. HLPC with a high sp. surface area (SSA) up to 2725 m2 g-1 is made up of interconnected microporous carbon walls.  Chem. anal. shows that the HLPC is doped with nitrogen and also has oxygen-contg. groups.  Electrochem. measurements show that the HLPC not only exhibits a high specific capacitance of 342 F g-1 and 171 F cm-3 at 0.2 A g-1 but also shows considerable rate capability with a retention of 62% at 20 A g-1 as well as good cycling performance with 98% retention over 1000 cycles at 10 A g-1 in 6 M KOH.  Furthermore, an as-fabricated HLPC-based sym. SC device delivers a max. energy d. of ∼9.4 Wh kg-1 in the KOH electrolyte.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Hierarchical porous N-doped C (HPNC) nanosheets (NS) have been prepd. via simultaneous activation and graphitization of biomass-derived natural silk.  The as-obtained HPNC-NS show favorable features for electrochem. energy storage such as high sp. surface area (SBET: 2494 m2/g), high vol. of hierarchical pores (2.28 cm3/g), nanosheet structures, rich N-doping (4.7%), and defects. The as-prepd. N-CNFs were used as anode material for sodium-ion batteries due to their unique fabric and weakly-ordered turbostratic structure as well as large spacing between graphene layers.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this study, highly nanoporous carbon (HCl-TW-Car) was successfully synthesized using a facile procedure combining acid treatment with a carbonization process that uses waste tea leaves from spent tea bags as raw materials.  The acid treatment not only promotes the efficient removal of unnecessary inorg. impurities but also increases the product porosity to enable synthesis of hierarchically porous carbon materials with various micro-, meso-, and macropores.  When used as an anode material for lithium-ion batteries, HCl-TW-Car demonstrated a much higher discharge capacity than is theor. possible using graphite [479 mAh g-1 after the 200th cycle at a rate of 0.2C (1C = 372 mA g-1)] and exhibited greater rate capabilities compared with those of carbonated products from tea waste without acid treatment.  It was shown that the good electrochem. properties of HCl-TW-Car can be ascribed to large Brunauer-Emmett-Teller (BET) surface area, well-formed hierarchical pores, and the prevention of unexpected electrochem. reactions from the redn. of metallic atoms.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq29778jABQQLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxV1qNWHpUCw"> &gt;&gt;         </div><div class="casAbstract">Anode materials with capacitive charge storage (CCS) are highly desirable for the development of high-performance Na-ion batteries (SIBs), because the capacitive process usually shows kinetically high ion diffusion and superior structural stability.  Here, the authors report a new CCS anode material of graphene-based N-doped C sandwich nanosheets (G-NCs).  The as-prepd. G-NCs show a high capacitive contribution during the discharge/charge processes.  As expected, the G-NCs exhibit excellent rate performance with a reversible capacity of 110 mA-h g-1, even at a current ≤10,000 mA g-1, and outstanding cycle stability (a retention of 154 mA-h g-1 after 10,000 cycles at 5000 mA g-1).  This represents the best cycle stability among all reported C anode materials for SIBs, thereby showing great potential as a com. anode material for SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpNTDDG2gGJs7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhxV1qNWHpUCw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XntFGgurY%253D&amp;md5=cc7a081eb16dcab861ba88f52cd78a32</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref36"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref36" class="rightTabRefNumLink">36</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit36" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.04.040"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Liu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Jia, M.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, B.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Lv, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Tang, R.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wu, F.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xu, B.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Nitrogen-doped Carbon/graphene Hybrid Anode Material for Sodium-ion Batteries with Excellent Rate Capability</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped carbon/graphene (NCG) hybrid materials were prepd. by an in-situ polymn. and followed pyrolysis for sodium-ion batteries.  The NCG has a large interlayer distance (0.360 nm) and a high nitrogen content of 7.54 at%, resulting in a high reversible sodium storage capacity of 336 mAh/g at 30 mA/g.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Enhancing the nitrogen (N) doping in carbon nanomaterials has been suggested as an effective approach to enhance the performance of lithium ion batteries (LIBs).  However, achieving N-doped carbon nanomaterials with an ultrahigh N content is still a great challenge, thus limiting the capacity enhancement.  Herein, we demonstrate a new procedure for the synthesis of unique sandwich architecture of N-doped carbon/reduced graphene oxide (N-carbon/rGO) derived from simple pyrolysis of a polypyrrole/GO nanosheet precursor.  The N-carbon/rGO exhibits the highest N-doping of 15.4% reported in all the carbon-based nanomaterials, and a high sp. surface area of 327 m2 g-1 with a micro/mesoporous structure.  They combine the advantages of high cond. of rGO, very high N-functionalities, and the porous structure of carbons, which endow them with appealing electrochem. lithium storage properties with a high initial reversible capacity of 1100 mA h g-1 at 100 mA g-1, excellent rate capability up to 20 A g-1, and superior cycling stability over 1000 cycles at a high c.d. of 1 A g-1.  The present work highlights the important role of tuning the nitrogen doping in enhancing the performance of LIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoCjCHAlSOj3rVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUjGQF6hTSqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XnsF2mtw%253D%253D&amp;md5=60b41095b6fdbbb830bae62cfc93f035</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref38"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref38" class="rightTabRefNumLink">38</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit38" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2016.08.096"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Chen, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Meng, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xie, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, D.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lithium and Sodium Storage in Highly Ordered Mesoporous Nitrogen-doped Carbons Derived from Honey</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Honey, a widely existent biomass, consists mainly of carbohydrate and other N-contg. substances such as proteins, enzymes and org. acids.  It can be mixed homogeneously with mesoporous SiO2 template for its excellent H2O-soly. and moderate viscosity.  Honey was employed as a N-contg. C precursor to prep. N-doped ordered mesoporous carbons (OMCs).  The obtained honey derived mesoporous N-doped carbons (HMNCs) with dilated interlayer spacings of 0.387-0.395 nm, narrow pore size distributions centering at ∼4 nm and satisfactory N contents of 1.38-4.32% offer superb dual functionality for Li-ion battery (LIB) and Na-ion battery (NIB) anodes.         </div><div class="casAbstract">For the common concern that general lignin-based colloidal spheres suffer the weakness of spherical structure destruction during the pyrolysis process, novel uniform lignin-derived nitrogen-doped carbon nanospheres were prepd. by direct pyrolysis of lignin-based azo polymer (AL-azo-NO2) colloidal spheres at 750 °C.  In addn., a kind of hard carbon with high graphitization degree was also prepd. as a control by direct pyrolysis of alkali lignin (AL).  The morphol. and structure of the as-obtained carbon materials were investigated by field emission SEM, X-ray diffraction patterns, Raman spectra and elemental anal.  They served as anodes in lithium-ion batteries with the aim to investigate the electrochem. performance.  These two kinds of lignin-derived carbon materials exhibited different electrochem. performances due to their various structures and functional groups.  The nitrogen-doped carbon nanospheres (CSAN-750) exhibited a high cyclic stable capacity up to 225 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 60 mA g-1 after 50 cycles (CAL-750, 120 mA h g-1) coupled with high first coulombic efficiency up to 66.4% for CSAN-3000 with a cyclic capacity of 200 mA h g-1, which is more comparable to that of the CAL-3000 (53.3%, 199 mA h g-1).                         rightTab-cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Naturally nitrogen doped porous carbon derived from waste shrimp shells for high-performance lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mondal, Anjon Kumar; Kretschmer, Katja; Zhao, Yufei; Liu, Hao; Fan, Hongbo; Wang, Guoxiu</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Microporous and Mesoporous Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Transformation of biomass wastes into sustainable low cost carbon materials is now a topic of great interest.  Here, we describe porous carbon from biomass derived waste shrimp shells and its application in two different energy storage systems.  The unique porous structure with the presence of heteroatoms (O, N) makes it promising material for both lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors.  When applied as anode materials for lithium ion batteries, the as-prepd. carbon showed a specific capacity as high as 1507 mA h g-1 and 1014 mA h g-1 at current densities of 0.1 A g-1 and 0.5 A g-1, resp., good rate performance and superior cycling stability.  The porous carbon-based supercapacitor also delivered a specific capacitance of 239 F g-1 at a c.d. of 0.5 A g-1 in 6 M KOH electrolyte.  The specific capacitance retention is 99.4% even after 5000 charge-discharge cycles, indicating excellent cycling stability.  The superior electrochem. performances for both lithium ion batteries and supercapacitors could be ascribed to the high sp. surface area, porous structure and nitrogen doping effect.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqBw8_YqwycCrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhUjGQF6hTSqw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXkvFymtbg%253D&amp;md5=a971ce97ed34a34dfb54e38000bbc80a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref41"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref41" class="rightTabRefNumLink">41</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit41" data-doi="10.1007/s13391-017-6223-5"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ou, J.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xi, X.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Porous Nitrogen Doped Carbon Derived from Horn Comb as Anode for Sodium-ion Storage with High Performance</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Electron.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The carbon material is regarded as the most promising anode candidate for sodium ion battery.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox active electrode materials derived from org. precursors are of interest for use as alternative cathodes in Li batteries due to the potential for their sustainable prodn. from renewable resources.  Here, a series of org. networks that either contain triazine units or are derived from triazine-contg. precursors are evaluated as cathodes vs. Li metal anodes as possible active materials in Li batteries.  The role of the mol. structure on the electrochem. performance is studied by comparing several materials prepd. across a range of conditions allowing control over functionality and long-range order.  Well-defined structures in which the triazine unit persists in the final material exhibit very low capacities at voltages relevant for cathode materials (&lt; 10 mA·h g-1).  Relatively high, reversible capacity (around 150 mA·h g-1) is in fact displayed by amorphous materials with little evidence of triazine functionality.  This result directly contradicts previous suggestions that the triazine unit is responsible for charge storage in this family of materials.  While the gently sloping discharge and charge profiles suggest a capacitive-type mechanism-further confirmed by the trend of increasing capacity with increasing surface area-ESR (EPR) spectroscopy studies show that the materials exhibiting higher capacities also display substantial EPR signals, potentially implicating unpaired spins in a charge storage mechanism that could involve charge transfer.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoLLZ7ezje3ZbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg9C4PA4x3fqA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXosFGntLk%253D&amp;md5=90dd8be697055066bd4e67619ae6eb20</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref51"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref51" class="rightTabRefNumLink">51</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit51" data-doi="10.1039/C5EE02574E"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Schwinghammer, K.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Hug, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Mesch, M.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The design of stable, yet highly tunable org. photocatalysts which orchestrate multi-step electron transfer reactions is at the heart of the newly emerging field of polymer photocatalysis.  Covalent triazine frameworks such as the archetypal CTF-1 have been theorized to constitute a new class of photocatalytically active polymers for light-driven water splitting.  Here, we revisit the ionothermal synthesis of CTF-1 by trimerization of 1,4-dicyanobenzene catalyzed by the Lewis acid zinc chloride and demonstrate that the microporous black polymer CTF-1 is essentially inactive for hydrogen evolution.  Instead, highly photoactive phenyl-triazine oligomers (PTOs) with higher crystallinity as compared to CTF-1 are obtained by lowering the reaction temp. to 300 °C and prolonging the reaction time to &gt;150 h.  The low reaction temp. of the PTOs largely prevents incipient carbonization and thus results in a carbon-to-nitrogen wt. ratio close to the theor. value of 3.43.  The oligomers were characterized by MALDI-TOF and quant. solid-state NMR spectroscopy, revealing variations in size, connectivity and thus nitrile-to-triazine ratios depending on the initial precursor diln.  The most active PTO samples efficiently and stably reduce water to hydrogen with an av. rate of 1076 (±278) μmol h-1 g-1 under simulated sunlight illumination, which is competitive with the best carbon nitride-based and purely org. photocatalysts.  The photocatalytic activity of the PTOs is found to sensitively depend on the polymn. degree, thus suggesting a prominent role of the unreacted nitrile moieties in the photocatalytic process.  Notably, PTOs even show moderate hydrogen prodn. without the addn. of any co-catalyst.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGox92N4Z0ZAJLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lj62Jz0uAzubA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXhsV2lt7nL&amp;md5=ef3692a27182894f48c1c31f87990a2e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref52" class="rightTabRefNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit52" data-doi="10.1021/la403366e"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Bhattacharjya, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Park, H.
